<div id="review_1291200722" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1291200722" />
    <a title="Denisse" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8759700-denisse"><img alt="Denisse" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1606102662p2/8759700.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1291200722?book_show_action=true">May 27, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Denisse" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Denisse" href="/user/show/8759700-denisse">Denisse</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">New Adult fans </span></div>

        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1291200722" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8387829943557745438"><b>Buddy-Read at the Emma's Tea Party.</b> Crazy group, full of BR, we can't deal with all of them. But we kick ass too ;) <br/><br/><b>Read for the 2015 Reading Challenge: #34 A book with a love triangle. And for my 2015 Reading Resolutions: 3 New Adult</b> (3/3) completed! <br/><br/><b>4.5</b> Color me surprised. I really liked Unravel. I was <i>this</i> close to accept that I was never going to like the NA genre, and it might be true, but, this book made me realize there are some pearls out there worth reading. <b>Interesting, emotional and s</b></span>
  <span id="freeText8387829943557745438" style="display:none"><b>Buddy-Read at the Emma's Tea Party.</b> Crazy group, full of BR, we can't deal with all of them. But we kick ass too ;) <br /><br /><b>Read for the 2015 Reading Challenge: #34 A book with a love triangle. And for my 2015 Reading Resolutions: 3 New Adult</b> (3/3) completed! <br /><br /><b>4.5</b> Color me surprised. I really liked Unravel. I was <i>this</i> close to accept that I was never going to like the NA genre, and it might be true, but, this book made me realize there are some pearls out there worth reading. <b>Interesting, emotional and sexy with some brushstrokes of basic dark novel/psycho thriller now and then, while remaining NA and Contemporary in essence.</b> So, if you’re in search of something good in that genre. This is the book. <br /><br /><br /><i>
  <b>”Pay attention, I say with my eyes. Listen closely. Hang onto every word. But most of all, please believe me.”</b>
</i><br /><br />Después de <u>Mud Vein</u> y <u>After</u>, dos polos opuestos en el género NA, la verdad, había perdido todas mis esperanzas. Y muy probablemente termino gustándome mucho Unravel gracias a que no solo es NA si no que tiene cierto misterio psicológico bastante agradable e incluso cierto nivel de novela negra, en un formato bastante básico, pero que eleva el libro. <br /><br /><i>
  <b>”Wouldn’t it be lovely if everything in our imagination were real?”</b>
</i><br /><br />Naomi, esta en un hospital mental y quiere salir, y para eso deberá contar la historia completa de lo que paso en su último verano, sacando a la luz la verdad que la encerró ahí en primer lugar. <br /><br />Ya que este libro se mueve alrededor de un misterio bastante estándar (aunque muy bien manejado), no quiero dar a explicar muchas cosas, ya que podría spoilear algo y creo que el libro se disfruta <b>solo</b> si no sabes lo que va a pasar. <br /><br />Obviamente Read no es una escritora de misterio así que les recomiendo no darle muchas vueltas al libro mientras lo estén leyendo. No es mal misterio pero tampoco es la excelencia en inteligencia. Lo que si me atrevo a decir, es que es una buena escritora NA, <b>los típicos temas del genero estuvieron bien manejados y la psicología detrás de algunos de ellos</b> (sobretodo del principal con Lana) <b>se desarrollaron muy bien. </b><br /><br /><b>Calia Read sabe cambiar de aires</b> muy bien, podría saltar de una escena bastante intima y sexy a algo muy creepy y emocional con una destreza increíble. Y eso ha hecho que el libro se sienta mas fluido. <br /><br />Hay algo que llamare el <b>“triangulo amoroso perfecto”</b> en primera porque creo que se describe muy bien esos dos tipos de enamoramiento. El típico <i>me enamoro de mi amigo de la infancia</i> y el otro típico <i>puro físico</i> <s>if you know what I mean</s> *alza una ceja*, además que tuvo un final bastante interesante. Así que lo apruebo, aunque disfrute más las escenas con Max que con Lachlan (Dios!, que nombre tan feo). <br /><br />A mitad del libro la historia se estanca un poquito pero aun así se disfruta. Después toma fuerza con el final que es lo mejor de todo el libro. <b>Recomendado</b> si eres fan del genero pero <i>sobretodo</i> si no lo eres. <b>Una gran historia</b>, ágil, que no pretende sentirse superior y por consiguiente se disfruta mucho, con personajes variados y bien parados, <b>con un tema principal delicado pero bien desarrollado</b> y un final digno aunque algo rosa para mi gusto. <br /><br />Ciento que la autora quería escribir un NA pero no quería que fuera el típico libro así que le agrego ciertos toques psicológicos y dramáticos que mezclados que sus escenas pasaditas de tono se convierte en una lectura fascinante. <br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[No lo vi venir, aunque me esperaba que Lana o Max o ambos fueran imaginaciones suyas, pero no por las razones que fueron al final. Me dio muchisima cosita cuando piensa Naomi “Lana’s dad, not mine. My dad would never do that to me” yo estaba de <i>pobrecita Diooooooooos</i><br />Solo una duda: Ósea que todo lo de la fiesta donde “conoce” a Max y eso no paso, o si paso por con Lachlan y no se daba cuenta? Eso no lo entendí, y lo del departamento de Lana ósea lo fue a buscar ella sola o nunca lo fue a buscar o que rayos?  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span></span>
  <a data-text-id="8387829943557745438" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <td colspan="2">

<span id="freeTextContainer5354809298861793965">I am more picky with books like this than I am with most subjects that I read. What subject is that, you ask? I cannot say, you'll have to read it and find out. Anyway, I'm picky for a reason, so when I got this one I thought I figured out what was happening pretty early on...and I did (for a reason). Even though I sort of knew what was happening, I loved it. That doesn't happen often. Normally, once I think I know where a story is going, I either get bored, or don't end up "loving it". I haven'</span>
  <span id="freeText5354809298861793965" style="display:none">I am more picky with books like this than I am with most subjects that I read. What subject is that, you ask? I cannot say, you'll have to read it and find out. Anyway, I'm picky for a reason, so when I got this one I thought I figured out what was happening pretty early on...and I did (for a reason). Even though I sort of knew what was happening, I loved it. That doesn't happen often. Normally, once I think I know where a story is going, I either get bored, or don't end up "loving it". I haven't read Calia's other books, but I'm going to say it anyway: this is her best work yet. I'm so glad I made her send it to me. I'm so glad I read it and I will definitely be reading it again. <br /><br />*note: this review is as cryptic as the book itself. Because I'm being mysterious about it, I'll describe it in a few words:<br /><br /><b> bold <b><br /><i> sexy <i><br /><b> beautiful <b><br /><i> mind fuckery <i><br /></i></i></b></b></i></i></b></b></span>

<div id="review_865630067" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/865630067" />

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/865630067?book_show_action=true">Feb 26, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Savina M." class="user" itemprop="url" name="Savina M." href="/user/show/27535698-savina-m">Savina M.</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27535698-savina-m?shelf=annoying-heroines">annoying-heroines</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27535698-savina-m?shelf=rolled-my-eyeballs-out">rolled-my-eyeballs-out</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27535698-savina-m?shelf=covers-i-like-to-fondle">covers-i-like-to-fondle</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27535698-savina-m?shelf=disappointing">disappointing</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27535698-savina-m?shelf=stupid-love-triangle">stupid-love-triangle</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27535698-savina-m?shelf=meh">meh</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27535698-savina-m?shelf=confusing-as-fuck">confusing-as-fuck</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27535698-savina-m?shelf=everyone-loves-it-but-me">everyone-loves-it-but-me</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27535698-savina-m?shelf=dafuq-was-that-ending">dafuq-was-that-ending</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer865630067" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2098431111797268307"><b>
  <u>How to write an <i>Unravel</i>: A Recipe</u>
</b><br/><br/><u>Ingredients:</u><br/><br/>1. Chapters-long flashbacks<br/>The first thing you'll need to write <i>Unravel Me</i> is not the actual madness of the protagonist. No—you'll need loads of confusing flashbacks that doesn't at all connect with your present protagonist. Therefore, readers won't have a sense of time reading. Make sure it's as confusing as possible!<br/><br/>2. A heroine who's 25, but <i>acts</i> 16<br/>Want your heroine to have loads of hot sex but also want her to connect with younger readers? No </span>
  <span id="freeText2098431111797268307" style="display:none"><b>
  <u>How to write an <i>Unravel</i>: A Recipe</u>
</b><br /><br /><u>Ingredients:</u><br /><br />1. Chapters-long flashbacks<br />The first thing you'll need to write <i>Unravel Me</i> is not the actual madness of the protagonist. No—you'll need loads of confusing flashbacks that doesn't at all connect with your present protagonist. Therefore, readers won't have a sense of time reading. Make sure it's as confusing as possible!<br /><br />2. A heroine who's 25, but <i>acts</i> 16<br />Want your heroine to have loads of hot sex but also want her to connect with younger readers? No worries, just state your heroine's age clearly, but make sure she <i>sounds</i> 16!<br /><br />3. Weird sex<br />Everyone knows New Adult has to contain sex. But how do you make yours stand out? Easy! Just change the setting of where your characters make love! Make them do it on the stairs! Against a tree! Of course, you still need the traditional on-the-bed. <br /><br />4. 17 times of lip sucking/biting/licking<br />Who doesn't love lip sucking? <s>I don't!</s> Make sure to add in lip sucking/biting/licking every time your characters make out, to totally <i>not</i> gross out your readers!<br /><br />5. 44 times of heart fluttering/doing flips/dancing/speeding up/thundering/racing/beating/pounding<br />Of course, your heroine's heart has to beat all the time because of all the hot sex. But you can't use "beat" all the time, because that would be repetitive. No worries, though, there's a perfect solution. Just search for all the synonyms for "beat", and your sentences can sound original as your heroine's heart pounds in her chest.<br /><br />6. Weird metaphors<br />It is most important that you paint a good picture for readers to imagine. You must shove in a metaphor every two sentences, even if the metaphor doesn't make sense.<br /><i>His lips were so close. It was like torture. Like dangling forbidden fruit in front of my face—I just wanted a single bite.</i><br /><br />7. Hot guy who only serves as a rich, fuck buddy for the heroine and to make a love triangle<br />A guy can only provide so much sex for the heroine. Therefore, you must have <i>two</i> heros in your story. Double the love-making!<br /><br />You've got all your ingredients? Good!<br /><br /><u>Cooking method</u><br /><br />Step 1: Mix all your ingredients together so they're all over the fucking place. Never mind if the readers don't get it. Because who cares about the timeline, right?<br /><br />Step 2: Add in an ounce of inconsistency of tenses.<br />I'm not talking about the switch of tenses between flashbacks and reality, I'm talking about the accidental change of tenses in one of the later chapters.<br /><br /><i>Tears <b>fell</b> from my face and onto the leather of the seat. Lachlan <b>didn't</b> brush them away and I <b>didn't</b> want him to brush them away.<br />I <b>dry</b> my face with the back of my hand and <b>sniffle</b>. I <b>look</b> over at Fairfax with dread.</i><br /><br />Step 3: Add a sudden change of POV<br />Throughout your entire book, there should only be Naomi (the protagonist)'s point of view, but shove in <br />another POV at 91%. Why not? Remember, your goal is to confuse the fuck out of readers.<br /><br />Step 4: Add in one single redeeming line, which is the only reason why the reader doesn't want to give it a one-star!<br /><i>"I love you too... But love doesn't solve everything."</i><br /><br />That folks, is how to fucking write an <i>Unravel</i>.<br /><br />Maybe I'm too stupid to get it. I don't know. I just wanted the book to end, so I didn't put much effort into reading the second half. Till now, I don't get why Naomi's the one who's crazy. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[She wasn't the one who got molested. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> By the end of the book I'm still left with a buttload of questions and that drives me crazy. I have a need for closure. <br /><br />I don't read a lot of contemporary, and I certainly don't read New Adult, which is probably why I don't like <i>Unravel</i>. Either way, <i>Unravel</i> has made sure I never touch New Adult again. <s>And the sex scenes also made me want to stay a virgin forever.</s></span>
  <a data-text-id="2098431111797268307" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

When you keep replaying scenes and rethinking all the amazing lines you read.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1443119485i/16320398._SY540_.jpg" width="350" height="350" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>I will not go into any details on the plot because this is something you most definitely need to go in to blind.     <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alienor ✘ French Frowner ✘" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alienor ✘ French Frowner ✘" href="/user/show/31461418-alienor-french-frowner">Alienor ✘ French Frowner ✘</a>

          added it




        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=dnf">dnf</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=2015-read">2015-read</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=in-a-minority-here">in-a-minority-here</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=dark">dark</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=new-adult">new-adult</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1250654485" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11670841507361467475">▶ <b>Here's my penance review because I feel bad - everybody seems to love this book, I wanted to join the club! <span id="freeTextContainer14833359198686569568"><i>My first thoughts: I knew it!<br/>Second: Disappointed.</i> <br/><br/>_____________________<br/><br/>The reason I am disappointed is because, somewhere along the way, I guessed what the mystery is, and when the big revelation came I was like: <i>Njah</i>. <br/><br/>I’m actually surprised with such high ratings this book has. It is by no means a bad book, but it’s not <i>that good</i>. I’ve read a few similar and better books in the past and I guess I was just not bewitched with this one as the rest. <br/><br/><a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[I am just – the clues were all th</span></span>
  <span id="freeText14833359198686569568" style="display:none"><i>My first thoughts: I knew it!<br />Second: Disappointed.</i> <br /><br />_____________________<br /><br />The reason I am disappointed is because, somewhere along the way, I guessed what the mystery is, and when the big revelation came I was like: <i>Njah</i>. <br /><br />I’m actually surprised with such high ratings this book has. It is by no means a bad book, but it’s not <i>that good</i>. I’ve read a few similar and better books in the past and I guess I was just not bewitched with this one as the rest. <br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[I am just – the clues were all there. The first thing I found suspicious was Max. There was something very insta-like in the way he and Naomi got together. I didn’t buy it. But the scene that screamed <i>What?!</i> to me was when he caught Naomi googling rape + Michael, he immediately knew it was about Lana. How, her name was not once mentioned. I think every sane person would assume it is about the person googling it – Naomi, not her friend. There was just something off about that whole ordeal. <br /><br />Also, I really don’t understand the point of his character. Was he <i>Max</i> only to Naomi or what? Did he know that she thought he was Max, and not Lachlan? How about when they first met? It’s just confusing.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />Also, the thing that bothered me so much – the switch to Dr. Rutledge’s POV at 90% mark. Just no. if you have the unreliable narrator, then stick to it. This felt like cheating.<br /><br />In the end, I’m left dissatisfied because of the way the book ended, I don’t think the author wrapped it up very well. A lot of loose ends and the way it concluded was kind of fairytale-like and unreal. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Lachlan killing Michael and getting away with it. Dr. Rutledge saving the day.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br /><u>Now, allow me to recommend:</u><br /><br />* When I first started reading <i>Unravel</i>, it reminded me so much to <b>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13557662.Insanity__Asylum___1_" title="Insanity (Asylum, #1) by Lauren Hammond" rel="nofollow noopener">Insanity</a>
</b> by Lauren Hammond (a girl in a mental institution without any recollection of how she got there, two love interests.. The similarities are there, but <i>Insanity</i> evoked more feelings in me.)<br /><br />* And, the <b>king</b> (or queen) <b>of all mind-fuck</b> – <b>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/2241059.Identical" title="Identical by Ellen Hopkins" rel="nofollow noopener">Identical</a>
</b> by Ellen Hopkins. I can’t say more without spoiling it, but that book, just wow. It will make you sick, it will make you question, it will make you put down your e-reader for a few minutes because.. you’re sane and that books is just not.<br /><br />In comparison to those two, <i>Unravel</i> is a baby.</span>

<div id="review_724818302" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/724818302" />
    <a title="Didi" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6082482-didi"><img alt="Didi" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1459297426p2/6082482.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/724818302?book_show_action=true">Sep 21, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Didi" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Didi" href="/user/show/6082482-didi">Didi</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6082482-didi?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6082482-didi?shelf=betrayal">betrayal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6082482-didi?shelf=friends-to-lovers">friends-to-lovers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6082482-didi?shelf=messes-with-your-head">messes-with-your-head</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6082482-didi?shelf=mental-health-issues">mental-health-issues</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer724818302" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11630389680654622241">4 STARS OR 8/10<br/><br/>WOW. This was crazy. Seriously crazy.<br/><br/>Unravel is one of those books that will probably haunt me for a long time. It was gutting and raw. It dealt with issues that we don't like hearing about. Because hearing about these things only reflects the basest, most hideous members of society, and knowing its hard to stop this is painful. I sound cryptic don't I?<br/>Saying more would be an injustice to this book and to the content within. It's best to read this with an almost blank slate. <br/><br/>While</span>
  <span id="freeText11630389680654622241" style="display:none">4 STARS OR 8/10<br /><br />WOW. This was crazy. Seriously crazy.<br /><br />Unravel is one of those books that will probably haunt me for a long time. It was gutting and raw. It dealt with issues that we don't like hearing about. Because hearing about these things only reflects the basest, most hideous members of society, and knowing its hard to stop this is painful. I sound cryptic don't I?<br />Saying more would be an injustice to this book and to the content within. It's best to read this with an almost blank slate. <br /><br />While at first I was confused and conflicted, deciding whether I found Naomi, our heroine, sane or not, it quickly became apparent that this was a very complicated story. There were a few pivotal scenes that helped me figure things out early on, but this did nothing to lessen the shock of the climax. I was still left appalled and shattered. Everything came together beautifully at a point where I felt it couldn't possibly be resolved. But it was and of course everything made sense. The only thing that didn't was leaving a certain plot twist unresolved. It left me wondering about things that were never explained.<br /><br />Our hero, Lachlan was there for Naomi when everyone else wasn't. He endured the pain right along with her and by the end I couldn't picture a better man. Other characters were incredible, mainly ones dealing with Naomi's care, but to elaborate would spoil everything. This isn't a dark romance or a suspenseful one either. It's a romance that delves into rarely talked about waters. It's a romance where tragedy could have festered, but didn't. Only with hope and the perseverance of 2 special people could Naomi break free. <br /><br />This isn't a long book but one that packs quite the punch. It left me feeling so many conflicting emotions that I finally breathed when it was all over. And you WILL breathe when it's all over because this will make you smile as much as it makes you shatter. Fantastic.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11630389680654622241" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_724819131" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/724819131" />
    <a title="Melissa" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9684061-melissa"><img alt="Melissa" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528750408p2/9684061.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/724819131?book_show_action=true">Sep 21, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Melissa" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Melissa" href="/user/show/9684061-melissa">Melissa</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer724819131" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13945032357462161865"><b>
  <i>“Most people believe the truth is a delicate little bird. They think it’s harmless.”</i>
</b><br/><br/>You know you’re reading a great book when you continuously ask yourself - what’s taken me so long to read this?! It’s confusing and frustrating, but the ending is so worth it.<br/><br/>Noami wakes up in a mental hospital and has no idea how she got there. Through a series of flashbacks, memories and even hallucinations, she starts to untangle the mess her life has become. Further confusing things are her feelings for t</span>
  <span id="freeText13945032357462161865" style="display:none"><b>
  <i>“Most people believe the truth is a delicate little bird. They think it’s harmless.”</i>
</b><br /><br />You know you’re reading a great book when you continuously ask yourself - what’s taken me so long to read this?! It’s confusing and frustrating, but the ending is so worth it.<br /><br />Noami wakes up in a mental hospital and has no idea how she got there. Through a series of flashbacks, memories and even hallucinations, she starts to untangle the mess her life has become. Further confusing things are her feelings for two guys - Max and her childhood love, Lachlan. I'm gonna stop there because the less you know the better.<br /><br />This book had me questioning every single thing! Naomi’s thoughts were incoherent half of the time, but it added a great element to the storyline. Even when I thought I had it all figured out, there were little things that nagged me and made me want to abandon my theory, but in the end I was partially right. I really, really liked how everything came together in the end.<br /><br />They only thing I wish was that the author had gone back and sort of fit everything together neatly - showed us how it all made sense. Instead, she left it up to the reader to do so. Overall, I thought this was a clever story.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13945032357462161865" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_862430094" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/862430094" />
    <a title="Paula " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2879703-paula"><img alt="Paula " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1536687412p2/2879703.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/862430094?book_show_action=true">Feb 22, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Paula " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Paula " href="/user/show/2879703-paula">Paula </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2879703-paula?shelf=new-adult-romance">new-adult-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2879703-paula?shelf=thriller-suspense">thriller-suspense</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer862430094" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4845266197183687132"><br/>What a fascinating, suspenseful, crazy book! It had me knots and made my head spin nearly the entire time. I do STRONGLY urge you not to skip to the last page or you’ll ruin the suspense and the buildup that leads to a shocking ending when the intricate storyline finally comes together. <br/> <br/>In the beginning of the story we meet Naomi Carradine, our heroine, who has been involuntarily committed in a mental institution. We don’t know why she’s there or what happen to her. What we do learn is that her</span>
  <span id="freeText4845266197183687132" style="display:none"><br />What a fascinating, suspenseful, crazy book! It had me knots and made my head spin nearly the entire time. I do STRONGLY urge you not to skip to the last page or you’ll ruin the suspense and the buildup that leads to a shocking ending when the intricate storyline finally comes together. <br /> <br />In the beginning of the story we meet Naomi Carradine, our heroine, who has been involuntarily committed in a mental institution. We don’t know why she’s there or what happen to her. What we do learn is that her world is unraveling around her. The doctors think Naomi is making up stories about the people in her life, that they aren’t real and only in her head. But she is adamant about the truth and wants her doctor to believe her, which led to a lot of unspoken questions swirling around in my head: Is this girl even sane? Why was she committed? What brought her to this point? These questions and other questions I had are answered as Naomi’s story is told. <br /><br />Naomi’s story alternates between the present, in the mental hospital, and the past. Naomi is in love with two men. Max is her current love interest. He’s the man who haunts her dreams and thoughts. And Lachlan is the boy next door she grew up with, forming a deep seeded connection with that turned into love. Then there is Lana, Naomi’s best friend, who is shy and meek. These best friends love each other something fierce and are always there for each other. Some bad things happen to Lana and Naomi tries to help. This sets things into motion that leads to Naomi being committed. <br /><br />I love both Max and Lachlan. Both of them are sexy, sweet, and loyal. Both of them came across as the epitome of perfect with the way they love and cherish Naomi. They are both different but alike at the same time. And they both own a piece of Naomi’s heart. Mine as well! But I won’t delve any further into the story. The less you know the better.<br /> <br />The build up to the story was a slow but intense, suspenseful ride and totally addictive. There is nothing like the feeling of not knowing what is about to happen yet dying to know at the same time. My thoughts were spinning all around in my head. It did take me nearly the first half of the book to catch on to the mystery that drove the storyline. But the things I never caught on to shocked the hell out of me. <br /><br />The romance element in the story is complex and beautiful and strong. It’s also an integral part of the story. The sex scenes are seriously raging hot! And very well-done! You’re probably wondering by now if this is a love triangle. That question will be answered as you read the story. My lips are sealed. *wink wink* But I will leave you with this quote I love…<br /><br /><i>
  <b>"My heart is stuck in my throat, as I look him over. I love him so much. I love him too much to be considered healthy. I know that."<br /><br />"Someday, you're gonna get out of here." He utters the last of his words slowly. "And everything's going to be okay."<br /><br />"Tell me what you're fighting and I'll fight with you."</b>
</i><br /><br />Now, I would be lying to say the subject matter in <i>Unravel</i> isn’t sensitive. Calia Read writes a raw and painful story that gutted me. I must warn you this story has a rape scene written in a discreet way but still very disturbing. If that type of dark content easily disturbs you, then this book isn’t for you. <br /><br />I loved <i>Unravel</i> because it was so different. It kept me engaged with the suspenseful and interesting storyline. There are a few questionable things about the story that seemed to be too easily resolved, but those things didn’t ruin the story for me. This book hooked immediately on the first page, making it impossible for me to put my Kindle down as I tried desperately to figure everything out. This book left an impression on me so much so that I continued to think about it for days after I was done with it. Go ahead and one-click this baby and get started because you don’t want to miss out on this one! <br /><br />Rating: B+<br />Heat: Hot<br /><br />-- <i>A <a href="http://romanticbookaffairs.blogspot.com/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Romantic Book Affairs</a> Review</i><br /><br /><br /><b>
  <i>Find us on <a href="https://twitter.com/rombookaffairs" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> and <a href="http://facebook.com/rombookaffairs" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> too!</i>
</b><br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="4845266197183687132" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('TWn/BgftiMvX0IGv0UI68WgcuFnmyohI5qbdoLBQtXF7OOJer1TE5+E7rHVVBVYFAiiI8xAU7EN2WNLcbAQmtQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('KME09h4qeHJJ2iJkHzUuzQBZOB537WNjMLxPlP/Gau4ekCmutpM0Xn8xD76bckI5am0ItIEzB2igQkDoI5L5Kg==')})
  }
